</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <small><i>(September 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Historically, Lutherans understand the Bible to present all doctrines and commands of the Christian faith <a href="/wiki/Clarity_of_scripture" title="Clarity of scripture">clearly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> In addition, Lutherans believe that God's Word is freely accessible to every reader or hearer of ordinary intelligence, without requiring any special education.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> A Lutheran must understand the language that scriptures are presented in, and should not be so preoccupied by error so as to prevent understanding.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> As a result of this, Lutherans do not believe there is a need to wait for any clergy, pope, scholar, or <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_council" title="Ecumenical council">ecumenical council</a> to explain the real meaning of any part of the Bible.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Efficacy">Efficacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Efficacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Lutherans confess that Scripture is united with the power of the Holy Spirit and with it, not only demands, but also creates the acceptance of its teaching.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> This teaching produces faith and obedience. Holy Scripture is not a dead letter, but rather, the power of the Holy Spirit is inherent in it.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> Scripture does not compel a mere intellectual assent to its doctrine, resting on logical argumentation, but rather it creates the living agreement of faith.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> As the <a href="/wiki/Smalcald_Articles" title="Smalcald Articles">Smalcald Articles</a> affirm, "in those things which concern the spoken, outward Word, we must firmly hold that God grants His Spirit or grace to no one, except through or with the preceding outward Word."<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sufficiency">Sufficiency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sufficiency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Lutherans are confident that the Bible contains everything that one needs to know in order to obtain salvation and to live a Christian life.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> There are no deficiencies in Scripture that need to be filled with by <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Tradition" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacred Tradition">tradition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obsequium_religiosum" title="Obsequium religiosum">pronouncements of the Pope</a>, new revelations, or present-day <a href="/wiki/Development_of_doctrine" title="Development of doctrine">development of doctrine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_Gospel">Law and Gospel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Law and Gospel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Lutherans understand the Bible as containing two distinct types of content, termed <a href="/wiki/Law_and_Gospel" title="Law and Gospel">Law and Gospel</a> (or Law and Promises).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> Properly distinguishing between Law and Gospel prevents the obscuring of the Gospel teaching of justification by grace through faith alone.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lutheran_confessions">Lutheran confessions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Lutheran confessions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bookofconcord.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/Bookofconcord.jpg" width="175" height="244" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="175" data-file-height="244" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bookofconcord.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Title Page from the 1580 <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Concord" title="Book of Concord">Book of Concord</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Book_of_Concord" title="Book of Concord">Book of Concord</a></i>, published in 1580, contains ten documents which some Lutherans believe are faithful and authoritative explanations of Holy Scripture. Besides the three <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Creeds" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecumenical Creeds">Ecumenical Creeds</a>, which date to <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman times</a>, the <i>Book of Concord</i> contains seven <a href="/wiki/Creed" title="Creed">credal</a> documents articulating Lutheran theology in the Reformation era.</p>
<p>The doctrinal positions of Lutheran churches are not uniform because the <i>Book of Concord</i> does not hold the same position in all Lutheran churches. For example, the <a href="/wiki/State_religion#Lutheran" title="State religion">state churches</a> in Scandinavia consider only the <i><a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Confession" title="Augsburg Confession">Augsburg Confession</a></i> as a "summary of the faith" in addition to the three ecumenical Creeds.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup> Lutheran pastors, congregations, and church bodies in Germany and the Americas usually agree to teach in harmony with the entire <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Concord" title="Book of Concord">Lutheran Confessions</a>. Some Lutheran church bodies require this pledge to be unconditional because they believe the confessions correctly state what the Bible teaches. Others allow their congregations to do so "insofar as" the Confessions are in agreement with the Bible.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Justification">Justification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Justification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg/220px-Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg" width="220" height="305" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg/330px-Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg/440px-Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2024" data-file-height="2805" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lucas_Cranach_d._%C3%84._-_The_Lamentation_of_Christ_-_The_Schlei%C3%9Fheim_Crucifixion_-_Alte_Pinakothek.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lutherans believe that whoever has faith in Jesus alone will receive salvation from the grace of God and will enter eternity in heaven instead of eternity in hell after death or at the second coming of Jesus.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The key doctrine, or <a href="/wiki/Formal_and_material_principles_of_theology" title="Formal and material principles of theology">material principle</a>, of Lutheranism is the doctrine of <a href="/wiki/Justification_(theology)#Lutheranism" title="Justification (theology)">justification</a>. Lutherans believe that humans are saved from their <a href="/wiki/Sin#Protestant_views" title="Sin">sins</a> by God's grace alone (<i><a href="/wiki/Sola_Gratia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sola Gratia">Sola Gratia</a></i>), through faith alone (<i><a href="/wiki/Sola_Fide" class="mw-redirect" title="Sola Fide">Sola Fide</a></i>), on the basis of Scripture alone (<i><a href="/wiki/Sola_Scriptura" class="mw-redirect" title="Sola Scriptura">Sola Scriptura</a></i>). Orthodox Lutheran theology holds that God made the world, including humanity, perfect, holy and sinless. However, <a href="/wiki/Adam_and_Eve" title="Adam and Eve">Adam and Eve</a> chose to disobey God, trusting in their own strength, knowledge, and wisdom.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pieper_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pieper-77">[75]</a></sup> Consequently, people are saddled with <a href="/wiki/Original_sin#Lutheranism" title="Original sin">original sin</a>, born sinful and unable to avoid committing sinful acts.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> For Lutherans, original sin is the "chief sin, a root and fountainhead of all actual sins."<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lutherans teach that sinners, while capable of doing works that are outwardly "good", are <a href="/wiki/Incurvatus_in_se" title="Incurvatus in se">not capable</a> of doing works that satisfy God's justice.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> Every human thought and deed is infected with sin and <a href="/wiki/Concupiscence" title="Concupiscence">sinful motives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> Because of this, all humanity deserves eternal damnation in <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_hell" title="Christian views on hell">hell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> God in eternity has turned His Fatherly heart to this world and planned for its redemption because he loves all people and does not want anyone to be eternally damned.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>To this end, "God sent his Son Jesus Christ, our Lord, into the world to redeem and deliver us from the power of the devil, and to bring us to Himself, and to govern us as a King of righteousness, life, and salvation against sin, death, and an evil conscience," as <a href="/wiki/Luther%27s_Large_Catechism" title="Luther's Large Catechism">Luther's Large Catechism</a> explains.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> Because of this, Lutherans teach that salvation is possible only because of the grace of God made manifest in the birth, life, suffering, death, and resurrection, and continuing presence by the power of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Spirit" title="Holy Spirit">Holy Spirit</a>, of Jesus Christ.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> By God's grace, made known and effective in the person and work of Jesus Christ, a person is forgiven, adopted as a child and heir of God, and given eternal salvation.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> Christ, because he was entirely obedient to the law with respect to both his human and divine natures, "is a perfect satisfaction and reconciliation of the human race," as the Formula of Concord asserts, and proceeds to summarize:<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>[Christ] submitted to the law for us, bore our sin, and in going to his Father performed complete and perfect obedience for us poor sinners, from his holy birth to his death. Thereby he covered all our disobedience, which is embedded in our nature and in its thoughts, words, and deeds, so that this disobedience is not reckoned to us as condemnation but is pardoned and forgiven by sheer grace, because of Christ alone.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Lutherans believe that individuals receive this gift of salvation through faith alone.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> Saving faith is the knowledge of,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup> acceptance of,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> and trust<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> in the promise of the Gospel.<sup id="cite_ref-Engelder_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Engelder-92">[90]</a></sup> Even faith itself is seen as a gift of God, created in the hearts of Christians<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> by the work of the Holy Spirit through the Word<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> and Baptism.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> Faith receives the gift of salvation rather than causes salvation.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> Thus, Lutherans reject the "<a href="/wiki/Decision_theology" title="Decision theology">decision theology</a>" which is common among modern <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">evangelicals</a>.</p>
<p>Since the term <i>grace</i> has been defined differently by other Christian church bodies (e.g. Roman Catholicism<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[95]</a></sup>) it is important to note that Lutheranism defines grace as entirely limited to God's gifts to us. Justification comes as a pure gift, not something we merit by changed behavior or in which we cooperate. Grace is not about our response to God's gifts, but only His gifts.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinity">Trinity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Trinity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg/220px-Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg.png" width="220" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg/330px-Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg/440px-Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="520" data-file-height="468" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shield-Trinity-Scutum-Fidei-English.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lutherans believe in the <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Trinity</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lutherans are <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Trinitarian</a>. Lutherans reject the idea that the <a href="/wiki/God_the_Father" title="God the Father">Father</a> and the <a href="/wiki/God_the_Son" title="God the Son">Son</a> are merely faces of the same person, stating that both the Old Testament and the New Testament show them to be two distinct persons.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[96]</a></sup> Lutherans believe the Holy Spirit proceeds from both the Father and the Son.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> In the words of the <a href="/wiki/Athanasian_Creed" title="Athanasian Creed">Athanasian Creed</a>: "We worship one God in Trinity, and Trinity in Unity; Neither confounding the Persons, nor dividing the Substance. For there is one Person of the Father, another of the Son, and another of the Holy Ghost. But the Godhead of the Father, of the Son, and of the Holy Ghost is all one: the glory equal, the majesty coeternal."<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Two_natures_of_Christ">Two natures of Christ</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Two natures of Christ">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Scholastic_Lutheran_Christology" title="Scholastic Lutheran Christology">Scholastic Lutheran Christology</a></div>
<p>Lutherans believe Jesus is the <a href="/wiki/Christ_(title)" title="Christ (title)">Christ</a>, the savior promised in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>. They believe he is both by nature God and by nature man <a href="/wiki/Hypostatic_union" title="Hypostatic union">in one person</a>, as they confess in Luther's <i><a href="/wiki/Luther%27s_Small_Catechism" title="Luther's Small Catechism">Small Catechism</a></i> that he is "true God begotten of the Father from eternity and also true man born of the Virgin Mary".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Confession" title="Augsburg Confession">Augsburg Confession</a></i> explains:<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote>
<p>[T]he Son of God, did assume the human nature in the womb of the <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Blessed Virgin Mary">blessed Virgin Mary</a>, so that there are two natures, the divine and the human, inseparably enjoined in one Person, one Christ, true God and true man, who was born of the Virgin Mary, truly suffered, was crucified, dead, and buried, that He might reconcile the Father unto us, and be a sacrifice, not only for original guilt, but also for all actual sins of men.</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sacraments">Sacraments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Sacraments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_sacraments" title="Lutheran sacraments">Lutheran sacraments</a></div>
<p>Lutherans hold that <a href="/wiki/Sacrament" title="Sacrament">sacraments</a> are <a href="/wiki/Sacred#Holiness_in_Protestantism" title="Sacred">sacred</a> acts of divine institution.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup> Whenever they are properly administered by the use of the physical component commanded by God<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> along with the divine words of institution,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup> God is, in a way specific to each sacrament, present with the Word and physical component.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> He earnestly offers to all who receive the sacrament<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> forgiveness of sins<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> and eternal salvation.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup> He also works in the recipients to get them to accept these blessings and to increase the assurance of their possession.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ArticleXIOfConfession.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ArticleXIOfConfession.JPG/220px-ArticleXIOfConfession.JPG" width="220" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/ArticleXIOfConfession.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="309" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ArticleXIOfConfession.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A.C. Article IX: Of Confession<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lutherans are not dogmatic about the number of the sacraments.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[110]</a></sup> In line with Luther's initial statement in his Large Catechism some speak of only two sacraments,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Baptism#Protestant_Reformation" title="Baptism">Baptism</a> and Holy Communion, although later in the same work he calls Confession and <a href="/wiki/Absolution#Lutheranism" title="Absolution">Absolution</a><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> "the third sacrament."<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> The definition of sacrament in the <i><a href="/wiki/Apology_of_the_Augsburg_Confession" title="Apology of the Augsburg Confession">Apology of the Augsburg Confession</a></i> lists Absolution as one of them.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> Since Absolution is a return to the forgiveness given in baptism, strictly speaking there are only two sacraments. <a href="/wiki/Confession_(Lutheran_Church)" title="Confession (Lutheran Church)">Private Confession</a> is not practiced among Lutherans as often as in the Catholic Church. Rather, it is expected before receiving the <a href="/wiki/First_Communion" title="First Communion">Eucharist for the first time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (May 2017)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Some churches also allow for individual absolution on Saturdays before the Eucharistic service.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A general confession and absolution (known as the <a href="/wiki/Penitential_Rite#Usage_in_Lutheranism" title="Penitential Rite">Penitential Rite</a>) is proclaimed in the Eucharistic liturgy. <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Lutherans do not emphasize "penance" as a retribution of sin but rather the proclamation of God's forgiveness by the "called and ordained" minister of the Holy Gospel.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baptism">Baptism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Baptism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Melanchthon-tauft.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Melanchthon-tauft.jpg/220px-Melanchthon-tauft.jpg" width="220" height="505" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Melanchthon-tauft.jpg/330px-Melanchthon-tauft.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Melanchthon-tauft.jpg/440px-Melanchthon-tauft.jpg 2x" data-file-width="642" data-file-height="1473" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Melanchthon-tauft.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German reformer <a href="/wiki/Philipp_Melanchthon" class="mw-redirect" title="Philipp Melanchthon">Philipp Melanchthon</a> baptizing an infant</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lutherans hold that <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">Baptism</a> is a saving work of God,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> mandated and instituted by Jesus Christ.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> Baptism is a "<a href="/wiki/Means_of_Grace#Lutheran_theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Means of Grace">means of grace</a>" through which God creates and strengthens "saving faith" as the "washing of regeneration"<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> in which infants and adults are reborn.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> Since the creation of faith is exclusively God's work, it does not depend on the actions of the one baptized, whether infant or adult. Even though baptized infants cannot articulate that faith, Lutherans believe that it is present all the same.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because it is faith alone that receives these divine gifts, Lutherans confess that baptism "works forgiveness of sins, delivers from death and the devil, and gives eternal salvation to all who believe this, as the words and promises of God declare."<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup> Holding fast to the Scripture cited in 1 Peter 3:21 "Baptism, which corresponds to this, now saves you, not as a removal of dirt from the body but as an appeal to God for a good conscience, through the resurrection of Jesus Christ."<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> Therefore, Lutherans administer Baptism to both infants<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> and adults.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> In the special section on <a href="/wiki/Infant_baptism" title="Infant baptism">infant baptism</a> in <a href="/wiki/Luther%27s_Large_Catechism" title="Luther's Large Catechism">his Large Catechism</a>, Luther argues that infant baptism is God-pleasing because persons so baptized were reborn and sanctified by the Holy Spirit.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eucharist">Eucharist</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Eucharist">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eucharist_in_the_Lutheran_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Eucharist in the Lutheran Church">Eucharist in the Lutheran Church</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JohntheSteadfast.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/JohntheSteadfast.JPG/220px-JohntheSteadfast.JPG" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/JohntheSteadfast.JPG/330px-JohntheSteadfast.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/2e/JohntheSteadfast.JPG/440px-JohntheSteadfast.JPG 2x" data-file-width="564" data-file-height="564" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JohntheSteadfast.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Luther communing <a href="/wiki/John,_Elector_of_Saxony" title="John, Elector of Saxony">John the Steadfast</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lutherans hold that within the <a href="/wiki/Eucharist_in_the_Lutheran_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Eucharist in the Lutheran Church">Eucharist</a>, also referred to as the Sacrament of the Altar, the Mass, or the Lord's Supper, the true body and blood of Christ are truly present "in, with, and under the forms" of the <a href="/wiki/Sacramental_bread" title="Sacramental bread">consecrated bread</a> and wine for all those who eat and drink it,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> a doctrine that the <i><a href="/wiki/Formula_of_Concord" title="Formula of Concord">Formula of Concord</a></i> calls the <a href="/wiki/Sacramental_union" title="Sacramental union">sacramental union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Conversion">Conversion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Conversion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RepentanceisContrition%26faith.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/eb/RepentanceisContrition%26faith.jpg/220px-RepentanceisContrition%26faith.jpg" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/eb/RepentanceisContrition%26faith.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="307" data-file-height="306" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RepentanceisContrition%26faith.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A.C. Article XII: Of Repentance</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In Lutheranism, conversion or regeneration in the strict sense of the term is the work of divine grace and power by which man, born of the flesh, and <a href="/wiki/Total_depravity" title="Total depravity">void of all power</a> to think, to will, or to do any good thing, and dead in sin is, through the gospel and holy baptism, taken from a state of sin and <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_death" title="Spiritual death">spiritual death</a> under God's wrath into a state of spiritual life of faith and grace, rendered able to will and to do what is spiritually good and, especially, made to trust in the benefits of the redemption which is in Christ Jesus.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>During conversion, one is moved from impenitence to repentance. The <i><a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Confession" title="Augsburg Confession">Augsburg Confession</a></i> divides repentance into two parts: "One is contrition, that is, terrors smiting the conscience through the knowledge of sin; the other is faith, which is born of the Gospel, or of absolution, and believes that for Christ's sake, sins are forgiven, comforts the conscience, and delivers it from terrors."<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Predestination">Predestination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Predestination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AugsburgConfessionArticle18FreeWill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/AugsburgConfessionArticle18FreeWill.jpg/220px-AugsburgConfessionArticle18FreeWill.jpg" width="220" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/AugsburgConfessionArticle18FreeWill.jpg/330px-AugsburgConfessionArticle18FreeWill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0b/AugsburgConfessionArticle18FreeWill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="346" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AugsburgConfessionArticle18FreeWill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A.C. Article 18: Of Free Will<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lutherans adhere to divine <a href="/wiki/Monergism" title="Monergism">monergism</a>, the teaching that salvation is by God's act alone, and therefore reject the idea that humans in their fallen state have a <a href="/wiki/Free_will_in_theology" title="Free will in theology">free will</a> concerning spiritual matters.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> Lutherans believe that although humans have free will concerning civil righteousness, they cannot work spiritual righteousness in the heart without the presence and aid of the Holy Spirit.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> Lutherans believe Christians are "saved";<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> that all who trust in Christ alone and his promises can be certain of their salvation.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to Lutheranism, the central final hope of the Christian is "the resurrection of the body and the life everlasting" as confessed in the <i><a href="/wiki/Apostles%27_Creed" title="Apostles' Creed">Apostles' Creed</a></i> rather than <a href="/wiki/Predestination" title="Predestination">predestination</a>. Lutherans disagree with those who make predestination—rather than Christ's suffering, death, and resurrection—the source of salvation. Unlike some <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinists</a>, Lutherans do not believe in a predestination to damnation,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> usually referencing "God our Savior, who desires all people to be saved and to come to the knowledge of the truth"<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup> as contrary evidence to such a claim. Instead, Lutherans teach eternal damnation is a result of the unbeliever's sins, rejection of the forgiveness of sins, and unbelief.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Divine_providence">Divine providence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Divine providence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to Lutherans, God preserves his creation, cooperates with everything that happens, and guides the universe.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> While God cooperates with both good and evil deeds, with evil deeds he does so only inasmuch as they are deeds, but not with the evil in them. God concurs with an act's effect, but he does not cooperate in the corruption of an act or the evil of its effect.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> Lutherans believe everything exists for the sake of the Christian Church, and that God guides everything for its welfare and growth.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>The explanation of the Apostles' Creed given in the <i><a href="/wiki/Luther%27s_Small_Catechism" title="Luther's Small Catechism">Small Catechism</a></i> declares that everything good that people have is given and preserved by God, either directly or through other people or things.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> Of the services others provide us through family, government, and work, "we receive these blessings not from them, but, through them, from God."<sup id="cite_ref-bookofconcord1_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bookofconcord1-146">[144]</a></sup> Since God uses everyone's useful tasks for good, people should not look down upon some useful vocations as being less worthy than others. Instead people should honor others, no matter how lowly, as being the means God uses to work in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-bookofconcord1_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bookofconcord1-146">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Good_works">Good works</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Good works">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg/220px-Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg/330px-Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg/440px-Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="748" data-file-height="999" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Die-Auferstahung-Christi_15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
"Even though I am a sinner and deserving of death and hell, this shall nonetheless be my consolation and my victory that my Lord Jesus lives and has risen so that He, in the end, might rescue me from sin, death, and hell."—<b>Luther</b><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Lutherans believe that <a href="/wiki/Good_works" title="Good works">good works</a> are the fruit of faith,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> always and in every instance.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> Good works have their origin in God,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> not in the fallen human heart or in human striving;<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> their absence would demonstrate that faith, too, is absent.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> Lutherans do not believe that good works are a factor in obtaining salvation; they believe that we are saved by the grace of God—based on the merit of Christ in his suffering and death—and faith in the Triune God. Good works are the natural result of faith, not the cause of salvation. Although Christians are no longer compelled to keep God's law, they freely and willingly serve God and their neighbors.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judgment_and_eternal_life">Judgment and eternal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Judgment and eternal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Primary_sources" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies too much on <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">references</a> to <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">primary sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please improve this section by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">secondary or tertiary sources</a>.</span> <small><i>(May 2017)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Lutherans do not believe in any sort of earthly <a href="/wiki/Millennialism" title="Millennialism">millennial</a> kingdom of Christ either before or after his second coming on the last day.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup> Lutherans teach that, at death, the souls of Christians are immediately taken into the presence of Jesus,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> where they await the second coming of Jesus on the last day.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup> On the last day,<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup> all the bodies of the dead will be resurrected.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>Their souls will then be reunited with the same bodies they had before dying.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> The bodies will then be changed, those of the wicked to a state of everlasting shame and torment,<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup> those of the <a href="/wiki/Imputed_righteousness" title="Imputed righteousness">righteous</a> to an everlasting state of celestial glory.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[159]</a></sup> After the resurrection of all the dead,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> and the change of those still living,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[161]</a></sup> all nations shall be gathered before Christ,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[162]</a></sup> and he will separate the righteous from the wicked.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>Christ will publicly judge<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> all people by the <a href="/wiki/Testimony" title="Testimony">testimony</a> of their deeds,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> the good works<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> of the righteous in evidence of their faith,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> and the evil works of the wicked in evidence of their unbelief.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> He will judge in righteousness<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> in the presence of all people and <a href="/wiki/Christian_angelic_hierarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian angelic hierarchy">angels</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> and his final judgment will be just <a href="/wiki/Damnation" title="Damnation">damnation</a> to everlasting punishment for the wicked and a gracious gift of life everlasting to the righteous.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comparison_among_Protestants">Comparison among Protestants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lutheranism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Comparison among Protestants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Protestant beliefs about salvation vary.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>This table summarizes the classical views of three <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Christian_soteriology#Distinct_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian soteriology">beliefs about salvation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup></p>
<center>
<table width="80%" cellpadding="5px" cellspacing="2" style="margin-bottom:1em; text-align:left; border:1px solid #444; margin:0 10px 0 10px;">
<tr style="background-color:#CEDFF9; text-align:center">
<th><b>Topic</b></th>
<th><b><a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a></b></th>
<th><b><a class="mw-selflink selflink">Lutheranism</a></b></th>
<th><b><a href="/wiki/Arminianism" title="Arminianism">Arminianism</a></b></th>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#eee;">
<td><b>Human will</b></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Total_depravity" title="Total depravity">Total depravity</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-Compare_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-Compare-176">[174]</a></sup> Humanity possesses "free will",<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> but it is in bondage to sin,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup> until it is "transformed".<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[177]</a></sup></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Total_depravity" title="Total depravity">Total depravity</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-Compare_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-Compare-176">[174]</a></sup> Humanity possesses free will in regard to "goods and possessions", but is sinful by nature and unable to contribute to its own salvation. <sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[178]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup></td>
<td>Humanity possesses freedom from necessity, but not "freedom from sin” unless enabled by "<a href="/wiki/Prevenient_grace" title="Prevenient grace">prevenient grace</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr style="background:#eee;">
<td><b>Election</b></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Unconditional_election" title="Unconditional election">Unconditional election</a>.</td>

<td><a href="/wiki/Conditional_election" title="Conditional election">Conditional election</a> in view of foreseen faith or unbelief.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup></td>

<tr style="background:#eee;">
<td><b>Justification and atonement</b></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Justification_by_faith" class="mw-redirect" title="Justification by faith">Justification by faith</a> alone. Various views regarding the extent of the atonement.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Unlimited_atonement" title="Unlimited atonement">Justification for all men</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-ROM_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-ROM-187">[185]</a></sup> completed at Christ's death and effective through <a href="/wiki/Sola_fide" title="Sola fide">faith alone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-TWB_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-TWB-188">[186]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WELS-Justification_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-Justification-189">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WELS-UnivJus_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-UnivJus-190">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup></td>
<td>Justification made <a href="/wiki/Atonement_(unlimited_view)#The_doctrine" class="mw-redirect" title="Atonement (unlimited view)">possible for all</a> through Christ's death, but only completed upon <a href="/wiki/Regeneration_(theology)#Arminian" title="Regeneration (theology)">choosing faith</a> in Jesus.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup></td>
</tr>

<td><b>Conversion</b></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Monergism" title="Monergism">Monergistic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup> through the means of grace, <a href="/wiki/Irresistible_grace" title="Irresistible grace">irresistible</a>.</td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Monergism" title="Monergism">Monergistic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-Diehl_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-Diehl-194">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> through the <a href="/wiki/Means_of_grace" title="Means of grace">means of grace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irresistible_grace#Lutheran" title="Irresistible grace">resistible</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-TULIP_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-TULIP-196">[194]</a></sup></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Synergism_(theology)" title="Synergism (theology)">Synergistic</a>, resistible due to the common grace of free will.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup></td>
</tr>

<td>Falling away is possible,<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-OSAS_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-OSAS-199">[197]</a></sup> but God gives gospel <a href="/wiki/Assurance_(theology)#Lutheranism" title="Assurance (theology)">assurance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WELS-Pers_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WELS-Pers-200">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup></td>
